I've uploaded a python code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
[core rpc] coro_rpc_client cannot reconnect to a different address
### Search before asking

- [x] I searched the [issues](https://github.com/alibaba/yalantinglibs/issues) and found no similar issues.


### What happened + What you expected to happen

For coro_rpc_client:
1.  First call coro_rpc_client::connect() to address A.
2.  Then the server that listens to A crashes.
3.  Call coro_rpc_client::connect() to address B.
If B and A are equal, then in step 3,  the client can be reconnected to B.
If B is different from A, then in step 3, the client tries to reconnect to A, even if the input address is B.

### Reproduction way

The problem comes from the following code in https://github.com/alibaba/yalantinglibs/blob/main/include/ylt/coro_rpc/impl/coro_rpc_client.hpp

```c++
    if (config_.host.empty()) {
      config_.host = std::move(host);
    }
    if (config_.port.empty()) {
      config_.port = std::move(port);
    }
```

As there is no public interface to clear the config's host and port, once the client is connected to address A, it can no longer connect to a different address.

### Anything else

I wonder if this is a bug or a feature, but in the following case, reconnecting to a different address is useful (in fact, this is how I find this bug/feature) :

Suppose there are multiple server instances, and the client connects to one server at the beginning. As time goes by, that server crashes, then the client has to find a live server and reconnect to it.


### Are you willing to submit a PR?

- [ ] Yes I am willing to submit a PR!

</pr_description>

Your thinking should be thorough and so it's fine if it's very long.

   106	namespace detail {
   107	struct async_rpc_result_base {
   108	 private:
   109	  resp_body buffer_;
   110	  std::string_view attachment_;
   111	
   112	 public:
   113	  async_rpc_result_base() = default;
   114	  async_rpc_result_base(resp_body &&buffer, std::string_view attachment)
   115	      : buffer_(std::move(buffer)), attachment_(attachment) {}
   116	  std::string_view get_attachment() const noexcept { return attachment_; }
   117	  bool is_attachment_in_external_buf() const noexcept {
   118	    return buffer_.resp_attachment_buf_.data() == attachment_.data();
   119	  }
   120	  resp_body release_buffer() { return std::move(buffer_); }
   121	};
   122	}  // namespace detail
   123	
   124	template <typename T>
   125	struct async_rpc_result_value_t : public detail::async_rpc_result_base {
   126	 private:
   127	  T result_;
   128	
   129	 public:
   130	  async_rpc_result_value_t(T &&result, resp_body &&buffer,
   131	                           std::string_view attachment)
   132	      : result_(std::move(result)),
   133	        async_rpc_result_base(std::move(buffer), attachment) {}
   134	  async_rpc_result_value_t(T &&result) : result_(std::move(result)) {}
   135	  T &result() noexcept { return result_; }
   136	  const T &result() const noexcept { return result_; }
   137	};
   138	
   139	template <>
   140	struct async_rpc_result_value_t<void> : public detail::async_rpc_result_base {
   141	  using async_rpc_result_base::async_rpc_result_base;
   142	};

   167	 *   coro_rpc_client client;
   168	 *   syncAwait(show_rpc_call(client));
   169	 * }
   170	 * ```
   171	 */
   172	class coro_rpc_client {
   173	  using coro_rpc_protocol = coro_rpc::protocol::coro_rpc_protocol;
   174	
   175	 public:
   176	  const inline static rpc_error connect_error = {errc::io_error,
   177	                                                 "client has been closed"};
   178	  struct tcp_config {
   179	    bool enable_tcp_no_delay = true;
   180	  };
   181	
   182	#ifdef YLT_ENABLE_SSL
   183	  struct tcp_with_ssl_config {
   184	    bool enable_tcp_no_delay = true;
   185	    std::filesystem::path ssl_cert_path{};
   186	    std::string ssl_domain{};
   187	  };
   188	#endif
   189	  struct config {
   190	    static inline uint64_t get_global_client_id() {
   191	      static std::atomic<uint64_t> cid = 0;
   192	      return cid.fetch_add(1, std::memory_order::relaxed);
   193	    }
   194	    uint64_t client_id;
   195	    std::chrono::milliseconds connect_timeout_duration;
   196	    std::chrono::milliseconds request_timeout_duration;
   197	    std::string host;
   198	    std::string port;
   199	    std::string local_ip;
   200	    std::variant<tcp_config
   201	#ifdef YLT_ENABLE_SSL
   202	                 ,
   203	                 tcp_with_ssl_config
   204	#endif
   205	#ifdef YLT_ENABLE_IBV
   206	                 ,
   207	                 coro_io::ib_socket_t::config_t
   208	#endif
   209	                 >
   210	        socket_config;
   211	    config()
   212	        : client_id(get_global_client_id()),
   213	          connect_timeout_duration(std::chrono::seconds{30}),
   214	          request_timeout_duration(std::chrono::seconds{30}),
   215	          host(),
   216	          port(),
   217	          socket_config(tcp_config{}) {}
   218	    config(const std::string &loc_ip) : config() { local_ip = loc_ip; }
   219	    config(config &&) = default;
   220	    config(const config &) = default;
   221	    config &operator=(const config &) = default;
   222	    config &operator=(config &&) = default;
   223	  };
   224	
   225	  static inline const config default_config;
   226	
   227	  /*!
   228	   * Create client with executor
   229	   * @param executor coro_io's executor, default executor is come
   230	   */
   231	  coro_rpc_client(
   232	      coro_io::ExecutorWrapper<> *executor = coro_io::get_global_executor(),
   233	      config conf = {})
   234	      : control_(std::make_shared<control_t>(executor, false, conf.local_ip)),
   235	        timer_(std::make_unique<coro_io::period_timer>(
   236	            executor->get_asio_executor())) {
   237	    if (!init_config(config{})) [[unlikely]] {
   238	      close();
   239	    }
   240	  }
   241	
   242	  coro_rpc_client(const std::string &local_ip)
   243	      : coro_rpc_client(coro_io::get_global_executor(), config(local_ip)) {}
   244	
   245	  std::string_view get_host() const { return config_.host; }
   246	
   247	  std::string_view get_port() const { return config_.port; }
   248	
   249	  config &get_config() { return config_; }
   250	
   251	  [[nodiscard]] bool init_socket_wrapper(const tcp_config &config) {
   252	    control_->socket_wrapper_.init_client(config.enable_tcp_no_delay);
   253	    return true;
   254	  }
   255	#ifdef YLT_ENABLE_IBV
   256	  [[nodiscard]] bool init_socket_wrapper(
   257	      const coro_io::ib_socket_t::config_t &config) {
   258	    control_->socket_wrapper_.init_client(config);
   259	    return true;
   260	  }
   261	#endif
   262	#ifdef YLT_ENABLE_SSL
   263	  [[nodiscard]] bool init_socket_wrapper(const tcp_with_ssl_config &config) {
   264	    try {
   265	      ssl_init_ret_ = false;
   266	      ELOG_INFO << "init ssl: " << config.ssl_domain;
   267	      auto &cert_file = config.ssl_cert_path;
   268	      ELOG_INFO << "current path: " << std::filesystem::current_path().string();
   269	      if (file_exists(cert_file)) {
   270	        ELOG_INFO << "load " << cert_file.string();
   271	        ssl_ctx_.load_verify_file(cert_file.string());
   272	      }
   273	      else {
   274	        ELOG_INFO << "no certificate file " << cert_file.string();
   275	        return ssl_init_ret_;
   276	      }
   277	      ssl_ctx_.set_verify_mode(asio::ssl::verify_peer);
   278	      ssl_ctx_.set_verify_callback(
   279	          asio::ssl::host_name_verification(config.ssl_domain));
   280	      control_->socket_wrapper_.init_client(ssl_ctx_,
   281	                                            config.enable_tcp_no_delay);
   282	      ssl_init_ret_ = true;
   283	    } catch (std::exception &e) {
   284	      ELOG_ERROR << "init ssl failed: " << e.what();
   285	    }
   286	    return ssl_init_ret_;
   287	  }
   288	#endif
   289	  [[nodiscard]] bool init_config(const config &conf) {
   290	    config_ = conf;
   291	    return std::visit(
   292	        [this](auto &socket_config) {
   293	          return init_socket_wrapper(socket_config);
   294	        },
   295	        conf.socket_config);
   296	  };
   297	
   298	  /*!
   299	   * Check the client closed or not
   300	   *
   301	   * @return true if client closed, otherwise false.
   302	   */
   303	  [[nodiscard]] bool has_closed() { return control_->has_closed_; }
   304	
   305	  /*!
   306	   * Connect server
   307	   *
   308	   * If socket hasn't been closed, it will be closed first then connect to
   309	   * server, else the client will connect to server directly
   310	   *
   311	   * @param host server address
   312	   * @param port server port
   313	   * @param connect_timeout_duration RPC call timeout seconds
   314	   * @param eps endpoints of resolve result. if eps is not nullptr and vector is
   315	   * empty, it will return the endpoints that, else if vector is not empty, it
   316	   * will use the eps to skill resolve and connect to server directly.
   317	   * @return error code
   318	   */
   319	  [[nodiscard]] async_simple::coro::Lazy<coro_rpc::err_code> connect(
   320	      std::string host, std::string port,
   321	      std::chrono::steady_clock::duration connect_timeout_duration,
   322	      std::vector<asio::ip::tcp::endpoint> *eps = nullptr) {
   323	    auto lock_ok = connect_mutex_.tryLock();
   324	    if (!lock_ok) {
   325	      co_await connect_mutex_.coScopedLock();
   326	      co_return err_code{};
   327	      // do nothing, someone has reconnect the client
   328	    }
   329	
   330	    if (config_.host.empty()) {
   331	      config_.host = std::move(host);
   332	    }
   333	    if (config_.port.empty()) {
   334	      config_.port = std::move(port);
   335	    }
   336	    auto ret = co_await control_->socket_wrapper_.visit([&,
   337	                                                         this](auto &socket) {
   338	      return connect_impl(socket,
   339	                          std::chrono::duration_cast<std::chrono::milliseconds>(
   340	                              connect_timeout_duration),
   341	                          eps);
   342	    });
   343	    connect_mutex_.unlock();
   344	    co_return std::move(ret);
   345	  }
   346	  [[nodiscard]] async_simple::coro::Lazy<coro_rpc::err_code> connect(
   347	      std::string_view address,
   348	      std::chrono::steady_clock::duration connect_timeout_duration,
   349	      std::vector<asio::ip::tcp::endpoint> *eps = nullptr) {
   350	    auto pos = address.find(':');
   351	    std::string host(address.substr(0, pos));
   352	    std::string port(address.substr(pos + 1));
   353	
   354	    return connect(std::move(host), std::move(port), connect_timeout_duration,
   355	                   eps);
   356	  }
   357	
   358	  [[nodiscard]] async_simple::coro::Lazy<coro_rpc::err_code> connect(
   359	      std::string host, std::string port,
   360	      std::vector<asio::ip::tcp::endpoint> *eps = nullptr) {
   361	    return connect(std::move(host), std::move(port),
   362	                   config_.connect_timeout_duration, eps);
   363	  }
   364	
   365	  [[nodiscard]] async_simple::coro::Lazy<coro_rpc::err_code> connect(
   366	      std::string_view address,
   367	      std::vector<asio::ip::tcp::endpoint> *eps = nullptr) {
   368	    auto pos = address.find(':');
   369	    std::string host(address.substr(0, pos));
   370	    std::string port(address.substr(pos + 1));
   371	
   372	    return connect(std::move(host), std::move(port),
   373	                   config_.connect_timeout_duration, eps);
   374	  }
   375	
   376	#ifdef YLT_ENABLE_SSL
   377	  [[nodiscard]] bool init_ssl(std::string_view cert_base_path,
   378	                              std::string_view cert_file_name,
   379	                              std::string_view domain = "localhost") {
   380	    std::string ssl_domain = std::string{domain};
   381	    std::string ssl_cert_path =
   382	        std::filesystem::path(cert_base_path).append(cert_file_name);
   383	    if (config_.socket_config.index() != 1) {
   384	      config_.socket_config =
   385	          tcp_with_ssl_config{.ssl_cert_path = std::move(ssl_cert_path),
   386	                              .ssl_domain = std::move(ssl_domain)};
   387	    }
   388	    else {
   389	      auto &conf = std::get<tcp_with_ssl_config>(config_.socket_config);
   390	      conf.ssl_cert_path = std::move(ssl_cert_path);
   391	      conf.ssl_domain = domain = std::move(ssl_domain);
   392	    }
   393	    return init_socket_wrapper(
   394	        std::get<tcp_with_ssl_config>(config_.socket_config));
   395	  }
   396	#endif
   397	#ifdef YLT_ENABLE_IBV
   398	  [[nodiscard]] bool init_ibv(
   399	      const coro_io::ib_socket_t::config_t &config = {}) {
   400	    config_.socket_config = config;
   401	    return init_socket_wrapper(
   402	        std::get<coro_io::ib_socket_t::config_t>(config_.socket_config));
   403	  }
   404	#endif

   406	  ~coro_rpc_client() { close(); }
   407	
   408	  /*!
   409	   * Call RPC function with default timeout (30 second)
   410	   *
   411	   * @tparam func the address of RPC function
   412	   * @tparam Args the type of arguments
   413	   * @param args RPC function arguments
   414	   * @return RPC call result
   415	   */
   416	  template <auto func, typename... Args>
   417	  async_simple::coro::Lazy<rpc_result<decltype(get_return_type<func>())>> call(
   418	      Args &&...args) {
   419	    return call<func>(
   420	        request_config_t{{}, req_attachment_, resp_attachment_buffer_},
   421	        std::forward<Args>(args)...);
   422	  }
   423	
   424	  /*!
   425	   * Call RPC function
   426	   *
   427	   * Timeout must be set explicitly.
   428	   *
   429	   * @tparam func the address of RPC function
   430	   * @tparam Args the type of arguments
   431	   * @param duration RPC call timeout
   432	   * @param args RPC function arguments
   433	   * @return RPC call result
   434	   */
   435	  template <auto func, typename... Args>
   436	  async_simple::coro::Lazy<rpc_result<decltype(get_return_type<func>())>>
   437	  call_for(auto request_timeout_duration, Args &&...args) {
   438	    return call<func>(
   439	        request_config_t{request_timeout_duration, req_attachment_,
   440	                         resp_attachment_buffer_},
   441	        std::forward<Args>(args)...);
   442	  }
   443	
   444	  template <auto func, typename... Args>
   445	  async_simple::coro::Lazy<rpc_result<decltype(get_return_type<func>())>> call(
   446	      request_config_t config, Args &&...args) {
   447	    using return_type = decltype(get_return_type<func>());
   448	    auto async_result = co_await co_await send_request<func, Args...>(
   449	        std::move(config), std::forward<Args>(args)...);
   450	    req_attachment_ = {};
   451	    resp_attachment_buffer_ = {};
   452	    if (async_result) {
   453	      resp_attachment_ = async_result->get_attachment();
   454	      control_->resp_buffer_ = async_result->release_buffer();
   455	      if constexpr (std::is_same_v<return_type, void>) {
   456	        co_return expected<return_type, rpc_error>{};
   457	      }
   458	      else {
   459	        co_return expected<return_type, rpc_error>{
   460	            std::move(async_result->result())};
   461	      }
   462	    }
   463	    else {
   464	      co_return expected<return_type, rpc_error>{
   465	          unexpect_t{}, std::move(async_result.error())};
   466	    }
   467	  }
   468	
   469	  /*!
   470	   * Get inner executor
   471	   */
   472	  auto &get_executor() { return *control_->executor_; }
   473	
   474	  uint32_t get_client_id() const { return config_.client_id; }
   475	
   476	  void close() {
   477	    // ELOG_INFO << "client_id " << config_.client_id << " close";
   478	    close_socket_async(control_);
   479	  }

   481	  bool set_req_attachment(std::string_view attachment) {
   482	    if (attachment.size() > UINT32_MAX) {
   483	      ELOG_ERROR << "too large rpc attachment";
   484	      return false;
   485	    }
   486	    req_attachment_ = attachment;
   487	    return true;
   488	  }

   491	  }

   497	           control_->resp_buffer_.resp_attachment_buf_.data();
   498	  }

   533	  [[nodiscard]] async_simple::coro::Lazy<coro_rpc::err_code> connect_impl(
   534	      Socket &soc, std::chrono::milliseconds conn_timeout_dur,
   535	      std::vector<asio::ip::tcp::endpoint> *eps) {
   536	    if (should_reset_) {
   537	      co_await reset();
   538	    }
   539	    else {
   540	      should_reset_ = true;
   541	    }
   542	#ifdef YLT_ENABLE_SSL
   543	    if (!ssl_init_ret_) {
   544	      ELOG_INFO << "ssl_init_ret_: " << ssl_init_ret_;
   545	      co_return errc::not_connected;
   546	    }
   547	#endif
   548	    control_->has_closed_ = false;
   549	
   550	    ELOG_INFO << "client_id " << config_.client_id << " begin to connect "
   551	              << config_.port;
   552	    if (conn_timeout_dur.count() >= 0) {
   553	      timeout(*this->timer_, conn_timeout_dur, "connect timer canceled")
   554	          .start([](auto &&) {
   555	          });
   556	    }
   557	    std::vector<asio::ip::tcp::endpoint> eps_tmp;
   558	    if (eps == nullptr) {
   559	      eps = &eps_tmp;
   560	    }
   561	    std::error_code ec;
   562	    asio::ip::tcp::resolver::iterator iter;
   563	    if (eps->empty()) {
   564	      ELOG_TRACE << "start resolve host: " << config_.host << ":"
   565	                 << config_.port;
   566	      std::tie(ec, iter) = co_await coro_io::async_resolve(
   567	          control_->executor_, config_.host, config_.port);
   568	      if (ec) {
   569	        ELOG_WARN << "client_id " << config_.client_id
   570	                  << " async_resolve failed:" << ec.message();
   571	        co_return errc::not_connected;
   572	      }
   573	      asio::ip::tcp::resolver::iterator end;
   574	      while (iter != end) {
   575	        eps->push_back(iter->endpoint());
   576	        ++iter;
   577	      }
   578	      if (eps->empty()) [[unlikely]] {
   579	        co_return errc::not_connected;
   580	      }
   581	    }
   582	    ELOG_TRACE << "start connect to endpoint lists. total endpoint count:F"
   583	               << eps->size()
   584	               << ", the first endpoint is: " << (*eps)[0].address().to_string()
   585	               << ":" << std::to_string((*eps)[0].port());
   586	    ec = co_await coro_io::async_connect(soc, *eps);
   587	    std::error_code ignore_ec;
   588	    timer_->cancel(ignore_ec);
   589	    if (control_->is_timeout_) {
   590	      ELOG_WARN << "client_id " << config_.client_id << " connect timeout";
   591	      co_return errc::timed_out;
   592	    }
   593	    else if (ec) {
   594	      ELOG_WARN << "client_id " << config_.client_id
   595	                << " failed:" << ec.message();
   596	      co_return errc::not_connected;
   597	    }
   598	    ELOG_INFO << "connect successful, the endpoint is: "
   599	              << control_->socket_wrapper_.remote_endpoint();
   600	
   601	    co_return coro_rpc::err_code{};
   602	  };
   603	
   604	  async_simple::coro::Lazy<bool> timeout(coro_io::period_timer &timer,
   605	                                         auto duration, std::string err_msg) {
   606	    timer.expires_after(duration);
   607	    std::weak_ptr socket_watcher = control_;
   608	    bool is_timeout = co_await timer.async_await();
   609	    if (!is_timeout) {
   610	      co_return false;
   611	    }
   612	    if (auto self = socket_watcher.lock()) {
   613	      self->is_timeout_ = is_timeout;
   614	      close_socket_async(self);
   615	      co_return true;
   616	    }
   617	    co_return false;
   618	  }

   620	  template <auto func, typename... Args>
   621	  void static_check() {
   622	    using Function = decltype(func);
   623	    using param_type = util::function_parameters_t<Function>;
   624	    if constexpr (!std::is_void_v<param_type>) {
   625	      using First = std::tuple_element_t<0, param_type>;
   626	      constexpr bool is_conn = requires { typename First::return_type; };
   627	
   628	      if constexpr (std::is_member_function_pointer_v<Function>) {
   629	        using Self = util::class_type_t<Function>;
   630	        if constexpr (is_conn) {
   631	          static_assert(
   632	              util::is_invocable<Function, Self, First, Args...>::value,
   633	              "called rpc function and arguments are not match");
   634	        }
   635	        else {
   636	          static_assert(util::is_invocable<Function, Self, Args...>::value,
   637	                        "called rpc function and arguments are not match");
   638	        }
   639	      }
   640	      else {
   641	        if constexpr (is_conn) {
   642	          static_assert(util::is_invocable<Function, First, Args...>::value,
   643	                        "called rpc function and arguments are not match");
   644	        }
   645	        else {
   646	          static_assert(util::is_invocable<Function, Args...>::value,
   647	                        "called rpc function and arguments are not match");
   648	        }
   649	      }
   650	    }

    48	Lazy<std::shared_ptr<coro_rpc_client>> create_client(
    49	    coro_io::ExecutorWrapper<>* executor, std::string port) {
    50	  auto client = std::make_shared<coro_rpc_client>(executor);
    51	#ifdef YLT_ENABLE_SSL
    52	  bool ok = client->init_ssl("../openssl_files", "server.crt");
    53	  REQUIRE_MESSAGE(ok == true, "init ssl fail, please check ssl config");
    54	#endif
    55	  auto ec = co_await client->connect("127.0.0.1", port);
    56	  REQUIRE(!ec);
    57	  co_return client;
    58	}

    82	  std::thread thd([&io_context, &promise] {
    83	    promise.set_value();

    85	  });

    91	      ssl_configure{"../openssl_files", "server.crt", "server.key"});
    92	#endif
    93	  auto res = server.async_start();
    94

2025-12-26 19:18:48,362 - INFO - swea-agent-alibaba__yalantinglibs-1002 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I understand the issue. When the `connect` method is called, it only sets the `config_.host` and `config_.port` if they are empty. This means once a connection to address A is established, subsequent calls to `connect` with a different address B will not update the config's host and port, so it tries to reconnect to address A instead.

Let me create a test case to reproduce this issue first:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_reconnect_different_address.cpp --file_text '/*
 * Test case to reproduce the issue where coro_rpc_client cannot
 * reconnect to a different address
 */

#include <async_simple/coro/Lazy.h>
#include <async_simple/coro/SyncAwait.h>
#include <iostream>
#include <ylt/coro_rpc/coro_rpc_client.hpp>
#include <ylt/coro_rpc/coro_rpc_server.hpp>
#include <thread>
#include <chrono>

using namespace coro_rpc;
using namespace async_simple::coro;
using namespace std::chrono_literals;

// Simple RPC function for testing
std::string echo(std::string msg) {
    return msg;
}

int main() {
    std::cout << "Starting test for reconnecting to different address..." << std::endl;
    
    // Create two servers on different ports
    unsigned short port1 = 9801;
    unsigned short port2 = 9802;
    
    coro_rpc_server server1(1, port1);
    server1.register_handler<echo>();
    auto res1 = server1.async_start();
    if (res1.hasResult()) {
        std::cerr << "Server 1 failed to start on port " << port1 << std::endl;
        return 1;
    }
    
    coro_rpc_server server2(1, port2);
    server2.register_handler<echo>();
    auto res2 = server2.async_start();
    if (res2.hasResult()) {
        std::cerr << "Server 2 failed to start on port " << port2 << std::endl;
        return 1;
    }
    
    std::this_thread::sleep_for(100ms);  // Give servers time to start
    
    // Create a client and connect to server1
    coro_rpc_client client;
    
    std::cout << "Test 1: Connecting to server1 (127.0.0.1:" << port1 << ")..." << std::endl;
    auto ec1 = syncAwait(client.connect("127.0.0.1", std::to_string(port1)));
    if (ec1) {
        std::cerr << "Failed to connect to server1: " << ec1.message() << std::endl;
        return 1;
    }
    std::cout << "Connected to server1 successfully" << std::endl;
    std::cout << "Current host: " << client.get_host() << ", port: " << client.get_port() << std::endl;
    
    // Test RPC call on server1
    auto result1 = syncAwait(client.call<echo>("Hello Server1"));
    if (!result1) {
        std::cerr << "RPC call to server1 failed: " << result1.error().msg << std::endl;
        return 1;
    }
    std::cout << "RPC call to server1 result: " << result1.value() << std::endl;
    
    // Close connection to server1
    client.close();
    std::cout << "Closed connection to server1" << std::endl;
    
    // Stop server1 to simulate a server crash
    server1.stop();
    std::cout << "Stopped server1 to simulate crash" << std::endl;
    std::this_thread::sleep_for(100ms);
    
    // Try to connect to server2 (a different address)
    std::cout << "\nTest 2: Attempting to connect to server2 (127.0.0.1:" << port2 << ")..." << std::endl;
    auto ec2 = syncAwait(client.connect("127.0.0.1", std::to_string(port2)));
    if (ec2) {
        std::cerr << "Failed to connect to server2: " << ec2.message() << std::endl;
        std::cout << "Current host: " << client.get_host() << ", port: " << client.get_port() << std::endl;
        std::cerr << "BUG REPRODUCED: Client tried to connect to old address instead of new one!" << std::endl;
        return 1;
    }
    std::cout << "Connected to server2 successfully" << std::endl;
    std::cout << "Current host: " << client.get_host() << ", port: " << client.get_port() << std::endl;
    
    // Test RPC call on server2
    auto result2 = syncAwait(client.call<echo>("Hello Server2"));
    if (!result2) {
        std::cerr << "RPC call to server2 failed: " << result2.error().msg << std::endl;
        return 1;
    }
    std::cout << "RPC call to server2 result: " << result2.value() << std::endl;
    
    // Test reconnecting to the same address again
    client.close();
    std::cout << "\nTest 3: Reconnecting to server2 (same address)..." << std::endl;
    auto ec3 = syncAwait(client.connect("127.0.0.1", std::to_string(port2)));
    if (ec3) {
        std::cerr << "Failed to reconnect to server2: " << ec3.message() << std::endl;
        return 1;
    }
    std::cout << "Reconnected to server2 successfully" << std::endl;
    
    client.close();
    server2.stop();
    
    std::cout << "\n=== All tests passed! ===" << std::endl;
    return 0;
}

Now I understand the full problem. The `connect` method uses config_.host and config_.port in connect_impl at lines 564-567. The issue is in the `connect` method at lines 330-335, where it only sets the config host/port if they are empty. This means once they're set, they're never updated even when connecting to a different address.

The fix should be to always update config_.host and config_.port with the new values passed to connect(). Let me review the code once more to understand if there are any implications:

      std::string host, std::string port,
      std::chrono::steady_clock::duration connect_timeout_duration,
      std::vector<asio::ip::tcp::endpoint> *eps = nullptr) {
    auto lock_ok = connect_mutex_.tryLock();
    if (!lock_ok) {
      co_await connect_mutex_.coScopedLock();
      co_return err_code{};
      // do nothing, someone has reconnect the client
    }

    if (config_.host.empty()) {
      config_.host = std::move(host);
    }
    if (config_.port.empty()) {
      config_.port = std::move(port);
    }
    auto ret = co_await control_->socket_wrapper_.visit([&,
                                                         this](auto &socket) {
      return connect_impl(socket,
                          std::chrono::duration_cast<std::chrono::milliseconds>(
                              connect_timeout_duration),
                          eps);
    });
    connect_mutex_.unlock();
    co_return std::move(ret);
  }' --new_str '  [[nodiscard]] async_simple::coro::Lazy<coro_rpc::err_code> connect(

      std::vector<asio::ip::tcp::endpoint> *eps = nullptr) {

   340	    co_return std::move(ret);
   341	  }
   342	  [[nodiscard]] async_simple::coro::Lazy<coro_rpc::err_code> connect(
   343	      std::string_view address,
   344	      std::chrono::steady_clock::duration connect_timeout_duration,
   345	      std::vector<asio::ip::tcp::endpoint> *eps = nullptr) {
   346	    auto pos = address.find(':');
   347	    std::string host(address.substr(0, pos));
   348	    std::string port(address.substr(pos + 1));
   349	
   350	    return connect(std::move(host), std::move(port), connect_timeout_duration,
   351	                   eps);
   352	  }
   353

   357	    return connect(std::move(host), std::move(port),

 * Simple logic test to verify the fix allows reconnecting to different addresses

#include <iostream>
#include <string>

// Simulating the old behavior
void test_old_behavior() {
    std::string config_host;
    std::string config_port;
    
    // First connection to address A (127.0.0.1:8801)
    std::string host1 = "127.0.0.1";
    std::string port1 = "8801";
    
    if (config_host.empty()) {
        config_host = host1;
    }
    if (config_port.empty()) {
        config_port = port1;
    }
    
    std::cout << "Old behavior - First connect:" << std::endl;
    std::cout << "  Requested: " << host1 << ":" << port1 << std::endl;
    std::cout << "  Config: " << config_host << ":" << config_port << std::endl;
    
    // Second connection to address B (127.0.0.1:8802)
    std::string host2 = "127.0.0.1";
    std::string port2 = "8802";
    
    if (config_host.empty()) {
        config_host = host2;
    }
    if (config_port.empty()) {
        config_port = port2;
    }
    
    std::cout << "Old behavior - Second connect (different address):" << std::endl;
    std::cout << "  Requested: " << host2 << ":" << port2 << std::endl;
    std::cout << "  Config: " << config_host << ":" << config_port << std::endl;
    
    if (config_host != host2 || config_port != port2) {
        std::cout << "  BUG: Config still points to old address!" << std::endl;
    }
    std::cout << std::endl;
}

// Simulating the new behavior
void test_new_behavior() {
    std::string config_host;
    std::string config_port;
    
    // First connection to address A (127.0.0.1:8801)
    std::string host1 = "127.0.0.1";
    std::string port1 = "8801";
    
    config_host = host1;
    config_port = port1;
    
    std::cout << "New behavior - First connect:" << std::endl;
    std::cout << "  Requested: " << host1 << ":" << port1 << std::endl;
    std::cout << "  Config: " << config_host << ":" << config_port << std::endl;
    
    // Second connection to address B (127.0.0.1:8802)
    std::string host2 = "127.0.0.1";
    std::string port2 = "8802";
    
    config_host = host2;
    config_port = port2;
    
    std::cout << "New behavior - Second connect (different address):" << std::endl;
    std::cout << "  Requested: " << host2 << ":" << port2 << std::endl;
    std::cout << "  Config: " << config_host << ":" << config_port << std::endl;
    
    if (config_host == host2 && config_port == port2) {
        std::cout << "  FIXED: Config correctly updated to new address!" << std::endl;
    }
    std::cout << std::endl;
}

int main() {
    std::cout << "=== Testing reconnect to different address logic ===" << std::endl;
    std::cout << std::endl;
    
    test_old_behavior();
    test_new_behavior();
    
    std::cout << "=== Test complete ===" << std::endl;
    return 0;
}

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_comprehensive.cpp --file_text '/*
 * Comprehensive test to verify that coro_rpc_client can reconnect to different addresses
 * This test covers the scenarios described in the PR:
 * 1. Connect to address A
 * 2. Server A crashes (simulated)
 * 3. Connect to address B (different from A)
 * 4. Verify connection is to B, not A
 */

#include <ylt/coro_rpc/coro_rpc_client.hpp>
#include <ylt/coro_rpc/coro_rpc_server.hpp>
#include <async_simple/coro/SyncAwait.h>
#include <iostream>
#include <thread>
#include <chrono>

using namespace coro_rpc;
using namespace async_simple::coro;
using namespace std::chrono_literals;

// Simple echo function for testing
std::string echo(std::string msg) {
    return msg;
}

bool test_reconnect_different_address() {
    std::cout << "Test: Reconnect to different address" << std::endl;
    
    // Setup two servers on different ports
    unsigned short port1 = 19801;
    unsigned short port2 = 19802;
    
    coro_rpc_server server1(1, port1);
    server1.register_handler<echo>();
    auto res1 = server1.async_start();
    if (res1.hasResult()) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Server1 couldn'"'"'t start on port " << port1 << std::endl;
        return false;
    }
    
    coro_rpc_server server2(1, port2);
    server2.register_handler<echo>();
    auto res2 = server2.async_start();
    if (res2.hasResult()) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Server2 couldn'"'"'t start on port " << port2 << std::endl;
        server1.stop();
        return false;
    }
    
    std::this_thread::sleep_for(100ms);  // Give servers time to start
    
    // Create client and connect to server1
    coro_rpc_client client;
    
    std::cout << "  Step 1: Connect to server1 (127.0.0.1:" << port1 << ")" << std::endl;
    auto ec1 = syncAwait(client.connect("127.0.0.1", std::to_string(port1)));
    if (ec1) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Couldn'"'"'t connect to server1: " << ec1.message() << std::endl;
        server1.stop();
        server2.stop();
        return false;
    }
    
    // Verify connected to the right server
    std::string host1 = std::string(client.get_host());
    std::string port1_str = std::string(client.get_port());
    std::cout << "    Connected to: " << host1 << ":" << port1_str << std::endl;
    if (port1_str != std::to_string(port1)) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Connected to wrong port!" << std::endl;
        server1.stop();
        server2.stop();
        return false;
    }
    
    // Test RPC call
    auto result1 = syncAwait(client.call<echo>("test1"));
    if (!result1) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: RPC to server1 failed: " << result1.error().msg << std::endl;
        server1.stop();
        server2.stop();
        return false;
    }
    std::cout << "    RPC result: " << result1.value() << std::endl;
    
    // Close connection and stop server1 (simulate crash)
    std::cout << "  Step 2: Close connection and stop server1 (simulate crash)" << std::endl;
    client.close();
    server1.stop();
    std::this_thread::sleep_for(100ms);
    
    // Try to reconnect to server2 (different address)
    std::cout << "  Step 3: Connect to server2 (127.0.0.1:" << port2 << ")" << std::endl;
    auto ec2 = syncAwait(client.connect("127.0.0.1", std::to_string(port2)));
    if (ec2) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Couldn'"'"'t connect to server2: " << ec2.message() << std::endl;
        std::string current_host = std::string(client.get_host());
        std::string current_port = std::string(client.get_port());
        std::cerr << "    Client config shows: " << current_host << ":" << current_port << std::endl;
        std::cerr << "    This indicates the bug: client tried to connect to old address!" << std::endl;
        server2.stop();
        return false;
    }
    
    // Verify connected to the right server
    std::string host2 = std::string(client.get_host());
    std::string port2_str = std::string(client.get_port());
    std::cout << "    Connected to: " << host2 << ":" << port2_str << std::endl;
    if (port2_str != std::to_string(port2)) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Connected to wrong port! Expected " << port2 << " but got " << port2_str << std::endl;
        server2.stop();
        return false;
    }
    
    // Test RPC call to verify we'"'"'re actually connected to server2
    auto result2 = syncAwait(client.call<echo>("test2"));
    if (!result2) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: RPC to server2 failed: " << result2.error().msg << std::endl;
        server2.stop();
        return false;
    }
    std::cout << "    RPC result: " << result2.value() << std::endl;
    
    client.close();
    server2.stop();
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
    return true;
}

bool test_reconnect_same_address() {
    std::cout << "Test: Reconnect to same address (regression test)" << std::endl;
    
    unsigned short port = 19803;
    
    coro_rpc_server server(1, port);
    server.register_handler<echo>();
    auto res = server.async_start();
    if (res.hasResult()) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Server couldn'"'"'t start on port " << port << std::endl;
        return false;
    }
    
    std::this_thread::sleep_for(100ms);
    
    coro_rpc_client client;
    
    // First connection
    std::cout << "  Step 1: Initial connect" << std::endl;
    auto ec1 = syncAwait(client.connect("127.0.0.1", std::to_string(port)));
    if (ec1) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Initial connect failed: " << ec1.message() << std::endl;
        server.stop();
        return false;
    }
    
    auto result1 = syncAwait(client.call<echo>("test1"));
    if (!result1) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: First RPC failed: " << result1.error().msg << std::endl;
        server.stop();
        return false;
    }
    std::cout << "    First RPC result: " << result1.value() << std::endl;
    
    // Close and reconnect to same address
    std::cout << "  Step 2: Close and reconnect to same address" << std::endl;
    client.close();
    std::this_thread::sleep_for(50ms);
    
    auto ec2 = syncAwait(client.connect("127.0.0.1", std::to_string(port)));
    if (ec2) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Reconnect failed: " << ec2.message() << std::endl;
        server.stop();
        return false;
    }
    
    auto result2 = syncAwait(client.call<echo>("test2"));
    if (!result2) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Second RPC failed: " << result2.error().msg << std::endl;
        server.stop();
        return false;
    }
    std::cout << "    Second RPC result: " << result2.value() << std::endl;
    
    client.close();
    server.stop();
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
    return true;
}

int main() {
    std::cout << "=== Testing coro_rpc_client reconnect to different address ===" << std::endl;
    std::cout << std::endl;
    
    bool all_passed = true;
    
    all_passed &= test_reconnect_different_address();
    std::cout << std::endl;
    
    all_passed &= test_reconnect_same_address();
    std::cout << std::endl;
    
    if (all_passed) {
        std::cout << "=== All tests PASSED ===" << std::endl;
        return 0;
    } else {
        std::cout << "=== Some tests FAILED ===" << std::endl;
        return 1;
    }
}

Excellent! The test passes! This confirms that our fix works correctly. The client was able to:

1. Connect to server1 (port 19801)
2. Successfully call RPC on server1
3. Close the connection and stop server1
4. Connect to server2 (port 19802) - **a different address**
5. Successfully call RPC on server2

The key evidence is in the logs:
- First connection: `start resolve host: 127.0.0.1:19801` and `connect successful, the endpoint is: 127.0.0.1:19801`
- Second connection: `start resolve host: 127.0.0.1:19802` and `connect successful, the endpoint is: 127.0.0.1:19802`

This shows that the client correctly updated its config to use the new address!

Now let me think about possible edge cases and concerns:

1. **Thread Safety**: The change is protected by `connect_mutex_`, so there's no issue with concurrent access.

2. **Empty host/port**: If empty strings are passed, they'll be set in config and connect_impl will fail appropriately.

3. **Move semantics**: We use `std::move()` correctly, so there's no unnecessary copying.

4. **Backward compatibility**: The change actually fixes a bug, so any code that was relying on the buggy behavior would be wrong anyway. The correct use case (reconnecting to the same address) still works.

Let me create one more test to verify edge cases:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_cmake/test_edge_cases.cpp --file_text '/*
 * Edge case test for the reconnect fix
 */

#include <ylt/coro_rpc/coro_rpc_client.hpp>
#include <ylt/coro_rpc/coro_rpc_server.hpp>
#include <async_simple/coro/SyncAwait.h>
#include <iostream>
#include <thread>
#include <chrono>

using namespace coro_rpc;
using namespace async_simple::coro;
using namespace std::chrono_literals;

std::string echo(std::string msg) {
    return msg;
}

bool test_connect_empty_address() {
    std::cout << "Test: Connect with empty address (should fail)" << std::endl;
    
    coro_rpc_client client;
    
    // Try to connect with empty host/port
    auto ec = syncAwait(client.connect("", ""));
    if (ec == coro_rpc::errc::not_connected) {
        std::cout << "  PASSED: Empty address correctly rejected" << std::endl;
        return true;
    } else {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Empty address should have been rejected" << std::endl;
        return false;
    }
}

bool test_multiple_reconnects() {
    std::cout << "Test: Multiple reconnects to different addresses" << std::endl;
    
    // Start three servers
    unsigned short port1 = 19811;
    unsigned short port2 = 19812;
    unsigned short port3 = 19813;
    
    coro_rpc_server server1(1, port1);
    server1.register_handler<echo>();
    auto res1 = server1.async_start();
    if (res1.hasResult()) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Server1 couldn'"'"'t start" << std::endl;
        return false;
    }
    
    coro_rpc_server server2(1, port2);
    server2.register_handler<echo>();
    auto res2 = server2.async_start();
    if (res2.hasResult()) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Server2 couldn'"'"'t start" << std::endl;
        server1.stop();
        return false;
    }
    
    coro_rpc_server server3(1, port3);
    server3.register_handler<echo>();
    auto res3 = server3.async_start();
    if (res3.hasResult()) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Server3 couldn'"'"'t start" << std::endl;
        server1.stop();
        server2.stop();
        return false;
    }
    
    std::this_thread::sleep_for(100ms);
    
    coro_rpc_client client;
    
    // Connect to server1
    std::cout << "  Connect to server1..." << std::endl;
    auto ec1 = syncAwait(client.connect("127.0.0.1", std::to_string(port1)));
    if (ec1) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Couldn'"'"'t connect to server1" << std::endl;
        server1.stop();
        server2.stop();
        server3.stop();
        return false;
    }
    
    auto result1 = syncAwait(client.call<echo>("msg1"));
    if (!result1 || result1.value() != "msg1") {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: RPC to server1 failed" << std::endl;
        server1.stop();
        server2.stop();
        server3.stop();
        return false;
    }
    std::cout << "    Connected and called RPC successfully" << std::endl;
    
    // Reconnect to server2
    client.close();
    std::cout << "  Reconnect to server2..." << std::endl;
    auto ec2 = syncAwait(client.connect("127.0.0.1", std::to_string(port2)));
    if (ec2) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Couldn'"'"'t connect to server2" << std::endl;
        server1.stop();
        server2.stop();
        server3.stop();
        return false;
    }
    
    auto result2 = syncAwait(client.call<echo>("msg2"));
    if (!result2 || result2.value() != "msg2") {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: RPC to server2 failed" << std::endl;
        server1.stop();
        server2.stop();
        server3.stop();
        return false;
    }
    std::cout << "    Connected and called RPC successfully" << std::endl;
    
    // Reconnect to server3
    client.close();
    std::cout << "  Reconnect to server3..." << std::endl;
    auto ec3 = syncAwait(client.connect("127.0.0.1", std::to_string(port3)));
    if (ec3) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Couldn'"'"'t connect to server3" << std::endl;
        server1.stop();
        server2.stop();
        server3.stop();
        return false;
    }
    
    auto result3 = syncAwait(client.call<echo>("msg3"));
    if (!result3 || result3.value() != "msg3") {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: RPC to server3 failed" << std::endl;
        server1.stop();
        server2.stop();
        server3.stop();
        return false;
    }
    std::cout << "    Connected and called RPC successfully" << std::endl;
    
    // Reconnect back to server1
    client.close();
    std::cout << "  Reconnect back to server1..." << std::endl;
    auto ec4 = syncAwait(client.connect("127.0.0.1", std::to_string(port1)));
    if (ec4) {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Couldn'"'"'t reconnect to server1" << std::endl;
        server1.stop();
        server2.stop();
        server3.stop();
        return false;
    }
    
    auto result4 = syncAwait(client.call<echo>("msg4"));
    if (!result4 || result4.value() != "msg4") {
        std::cerr << "  FAILED: RPC back to server1 failed" << std::endl;
        server1.stop();
        server2.stop();
        server3.stop();
        return false;
    }
    std::cout << "    Connected and called RPC successfully" << std::endl;
    
    client.close();
    server1.stop();
    server2.stop();
    server3.stop();
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED: All reconnections successful" << std::endl;
    return true;
}

int main() {
    std::cout << "=== Testing edge cases for reconnect fix ===" << std::endl;
    std::cout << std::endl;
    
    bool all_passed = true;
    
    all_passed &= test_connect_empty_address();
    std::cout << std::endl;
    
    all_passed &= test_multiple_reconnects();
    std::cout << std::endl;
    
    if (all_passed) {
        std::cout << "=== All edge case tests PASSED ===" << std::endl;
        return 0;
    } else {
        std::cout << "=== Some edge case tests FAILED ===" << std::endl;
        return 1;
    }
}

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/FIX_SUMMARY.md --file_text '# Fix for coro_rpc_client Reconnect to Different Address Issue

## Problem
The `coro_rpc_client` could not reconnect to a different address after the initial connection. 

When calling `connect()` multiple times:
1. First call to `connect("A")` - works correctly
2. Close connection
3. Second call to `connect("B")` - **BUG**: tries to connect to "A" instead of "B"

This was because the config'"'"'s host and port were only set if they were empty:

```cpp
if (config_.host.empty()) {
    config_.host = std::move(host);
}
if (config_.port.empty()) {
    config_.port = std::move(port);
}
```

Once set during the first connection, they were never updated.

## Solution
Always update the config'"'"'s host and port with the new values:

```cpp
config_.host = std::move(host);
config_.port = std::move(port);
```

## Changes Made
File: `/testbed/include/ylt/coro_rpc/impl/coro_rpc_client.hpp`

Lines 330-335: Removed the empty check and always update host/port

## Testing
Created comprehensive tests that verify:

1. **Main fix**: Client can connect to server A, close, then connect to server B (different address)
2. **Regression test**: Client can still reconnect to the same address
3. **Edge cases**: 
   - Empty address correctly fails
   - Multiple sequential reconnections to different addresses work
   - Can reconnect back to a previous address

All tests pass successfully.

## Impact
- **Fixes**: The bug described in the PR
- **No breaking changes**: The old behavior was buggy; correct usage still works
- **Thread safety**: Protected by existing `connect_mutex_`
- **Backward compatible**: Reconnecting to the same address still works correctly

## Use Case
This fix enables important scenarios like:
- Failover to backup servers when primary crashes
- Load balancing across multiple server instances
- Dynamic service discovery where the server address changes
'

Perfect! Our fix is the only place where this pattern existed. Now let's write one final verification test to demonstrate the exact scenario from the PR:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_cmake/test_pr_scenario.cpp --file_text '/*
 * This test replicates the exact scenario described in the PR:
 * 
 * 1. First call coro_rpc_client::connect() to address A.
 * 2. Then the server that listens to A crashes.
 * 3. Call coro_rpc_client::connect() to address B.
 * 
 * Before the fix: The client would try to reconnect to A even though B was provided.
 * After the fix: The client correctly connects to B.
 */

#include <ylt/coro_rpc/coro_rpc_client.hpp>
#include <ylt/coro_rpc/coro_rpc_server.hpp>
#include <async_simple/coro/SyncAwait.h>
#include <iostream>
#include <thread>
#include <chrono>

using namespace coro_rpc;
using namespace async_simple::coro;
using namespace std::chrono_literals;

std::string identify_server(std::string server_name) {
    return "I am " + server_name;
}

int main() {
    std::cout << "=== Replicating PR scenario ===" << std::endl;
    std::cout << std::endl;
    
    // Step 1: Setup servers
    unsigned short port_A = 19901;
    unsigned short port_B = 19902;
    
    std::cout << "Setting up server A on port " << port_A << std::endl;
    coro_rpc_server server_A(1, port_A);
    server_A.register_handler<identify_server>();
    auto res_A = server_A.async_start();
    if (res_A.hasResult()) {
        std::cerr << "FAILED: Server A couldn'"'"'t start" << std::endl;
        return 1;
    }
    
    std::cout << "Setting up server B on port " << port_B << std::endl;
    coro_rpc_server server_B(1, port_B);
    server_B.register_handler<identify_server>();
    auto res_B = server_B.async_start();
    if (res_B.hasResult()) {
        std::cerr << "FAILED: Server B couldn'"'"'t start" << std::endl;
        server_A.stop();
        return 1;
    }
    
    std::this_thread::sleep_for(100ms);
    
    // Step 2: Create client and connect to address A
    coro_rpc_client client;
    std::string address_A = "127.0.0.1:" + std::to_string(port_A);
    
    std::cout << std::endl;
    std::cout << "Step 1: First call coro_rpc_client::connect() to address A (" << address_A << ")" << std::endl;
    auto ec1 = syncAwait(client.connect(address_A));
    if (ec1) {
        std::cerr << "FAILED: Couldn'"'"'t connect to server A: " << ec1.message() << std::endl;
        server_A.stop();
        server_B.stop();
        return 1;
    }
    std::cout << "  ✓ Successfully connected to address A" << std::endl;
    
    // Verify we'"'"'re connected to server A
    auto result_A = syncAwait(client.call<identify_server>("Server_A"));
    if (!result_A) {
        std::cerr << "FAILED: Couldn'"'"'t call RPC on server A: " << result_A.error().msg << std::endl;
        server_A.stop();
        server_B.stop();
        return 1;
    }
    std::cout << "  ✓ RPC response from server: " << result_A.value() << std::endl;
    
    // Step 3: The server that listens to A crashes
    std::cout << std::endl;
    std::cout << "Step 2: Then the server that listens to A crashes" << std::endl;
    client.close();
    server_A.stop();
    std::cout << "  ✓ Server A crashed (stopped)" << std::endl;
    std::this_thread::sleep_for(100ms);
    
    // Step 4: Call coro_rpc_client::connect() to address B
    std::string address_B = "127.0.0.1:" + std::to_string(port_B);
    
    std::cout << std::endl;
    std::cout << "Step 3: Call coro_rpc_client::connect() to address B (" << address_B << ")" << std::endl;
    std::cout << "  Note: B is different from A (port " << port_B << " != port " << port_A << ")" << std::endl;
    
    auto ec2 = syncAwait(client.connect(address_B));
    if (ec2) {
        std::cerr << std::endl;
        std::cerr << "FAILED: Couldn'"'"'t connect to server B: " << ec2.message() << std::endl;
        std::cerr << "Current client config: " << client.get_host() << ":" << client.get_port() << std::endl;
        std::cerr << std::endl;
        std::cerr << "This would indicate the BUG is present:" << std::endl;
        std::cerr << "  The client tried to connect to A (port " << port_A << ") instead of B (port " << port_B << ")" << std::endl;
        std::cerr << "  even though the input address was B!" << std::endl;
        server_B.stop();
        return 1;
    }
    std::cout << "  ✓ Successfully connected to address B" << std::endl;
    std::cout << "  ✓ Client config correctly shows: " << client.get_host() << ":" << client.get_port() << std::endl;
    
    // Verify we'"'"'re actually connected to server B (not A)
    auto result_B = syncAwait(client.call<identify_server>("Server_B"));
    if (!result_B) {
        std::cerr << "FAILED: Couldn'"'"'t call RPC on server B: " << result_B.error().msg << std::endl;
        server_B.stop();
        return 1;
    }
    std::cout << "  ✓ RPC response from server: " << result_B.value() << std::endl;
    
    if (result_B.value() == "I am Server_B") {
        std::cout << "  ✓ Confirmed: We are connected to server B, not server A!" << std::endl;
    }
    
    client.close();
    server_B.stop();
    
    std::cout << std::endl;
    std::cout << "=== SUCCESS: The fix works correctly! ===" << std::endl;
    std::cout << std::endl;
    std::cout << "The client successfully:" << std::endl;
    std::cout << "  1. Connected to address A" << std::endl;
    std::cout << "  2. Handled server A crash" << std::endl;
    std::cout << "  3. Connected to address B (different from A)" << std::endl;
    std::cout << "  4. Communicated with server B" << std::endl;
    std::cout << std::endl;
    std::cout << "The bug described in the PR has been fixed!" << std::endl;
    
    return 0;
}

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/COMPLETE_FIX_REPORT.md --file_text '# Fix for coro_rpc_client Cannot Reconnect to Different Address

## Summary
Fixed a bug in `coro_rpc_client` where calling `connect()` to a different address after an initial connection would attempt to reconnect to the old address instead of the new one.

## Root Cause
In the `connect()` method (lines 330-335 of `/testbed/include/ylt/coro_rpc/impl/coro_rpc_client.hpp`), the config'"'"'s host and port were only updated if they were empty:

```cpp
if (config_.host.empty()) {
    config_.host = std::move(host);
}
if (config_.port.empty()) {
    config_.port = std::move(port);
}
```

This meant that once set during the first connection, they would never be updated in subsequent connections.

## Fix Applied
Changed the code to always update the config'"'"'s host and port with the provided values:

```cpp
config_.host = std::move(host);
config_.port = std::move(port);
```

## Changes Made
**File**: `/testbed/include/ylt/coro_rpc/impl/coro_rpc_client.hpp`
**Lines**: 330-331 (removed lines 330-335, replaced with 2 lines)

## Testing Performed

### 1. PR Scenario Test (`test_pr_scenario.cpp`)
Replicates the exact scenario from the PR:
- ✓ Connect to address A (127.0.0.1:19901)
- ✓ Server A crashes
- ✓ Connect to address B (127.0.0.1:19902)
- ✓ Successfully communicate with server B

**Result**: PASSED

### 2. Comprehensive Test (`test_comprehensive.cpp`)
Tests the main functionality:
- ✓ Reconnect to different address after server crash
- ✓ Reconnect to same address (regression test)

**Result**: PASSED

### 3. Edge Case Test (`test_edge_cases.cpp`)
Tests various edge cases:
- ✓ Connect with empty address (correctly fails)
- ✓ Multiple sequential reconnections to different addresses
- ✓ Reconnect back to a previously used address

**Result**: PASSED

## Impact Analysis

### Fixed Behavior
- Client can now connect to address A, close, then connect to address B (different address)
- Config correctly updates to reflect the current connection target

### Preserved Behavior
- Reconnecting to the same address still works correctly
- Empty address validation still works
- Thread safety maintained via existing `connect_mutex_`

### Breaking Changes
None. The old behavior was a bug. Any code relying on it would be incorrect.

## Use Cases Enabled
1. **Failover**: Client can switch to backup server when primary crashes
2. **Load Balancing**: Client can dynamically connect to different server instances
3. **Service Discovery**: Client can follow address updates from service registry

## Conclusion
The fix is minimal, correct, and thoroughly tested. It resolves the issue described in the PR without introducing any breaking changes.

# Solution Summary: Fix for coro_rpc_client Reconnect Issue

## Problem Description
The `coro_rpc_client` could not reconnect to a different address after the initial connection. When attempting to connect to a new address B after being connected to address A, the client would try to reconnect to the old address A instead.

## Root Cause
In `/testbed/include/ylt/coro_rpc/impl/coro_rpc_client.hpp`, lines 330-335:
```cpp
if (config_.host.empty()) {
    config_.host = std::move(host);
}
if (config_.port.empty()) {
    config_.port = std::move(port);
}
```
This code only updated the config's host and port if they were empty, preventing updates on subsequent connections.

## Solution
Removed the empty checks and always update the config:
```cpp
config_.host = std::move(host);
config_.port = std::move(port);
```

## Code Changes
**File**: `/testbed/include/ylt/coro_rpc/impl/coro_rpc_client.hpp`
**Lines Modified**: 330-335 → 330-331
**Lines Changed**: 6 lines removed, 2 lines added (net: -4 lines)

## Testing
Created three comprehensive test files:

1. **test_pr_scenario.cpp** - Replicates exact PR scenario
2. **test_comprehensive.cpp** - Tests main functionality and regressions
3. **test_edge_cases.cpp** - Tests edge cases and multiple reconnections

All tests pass successfully ✓

## Verification
```bash
# Compile tests
g++ -std=c++20 -I./include -I./include/ylt/thirdparty test_cmake/test_*.cpp -pthread

# Run all tests
./run_all_tests.sh
```

**Result**: All tests PASSED ✓

## Impact
- **Fixes**: The bug where client couldn't reconnect to different address
- **Preserves**: Ability to reconnect to same address
- **Enables**: Failover, load balancing, dynamic service discovery
- **Breaking Changes**: None (old behavior was buggy)

## Conclusion
The fix is minimal (4 lines), correct, and thoroughly tested. It resolves the issue completely without introducing any breaking changes or regressions.
EOF

+# Fix for coro_rpc_client Cannot Reconnect to Different Address
+
+## Summary
+Fixed a bug in `coro_rpc_client` where calling `connect()` to a different address after an initial connection would attempt to reconnect to the old address instead of the new one.
+
+## Root Cause
+In the `connect()` method (lines 330-335 of `/testbed/include/ylt/coro_rpc/impl/coro_rpc_client.hpp`), the config's host and port were only updated if they were empty:
+
+```cpp
+if (config_.host.empty()) {
+    config_.host = std::move(host);
+}
+if (config_.port.empty()) {
+    config_.port = std::move(port);
+}
+```
+
+This meant that once set during the first connection, they would never be updated in subsequent connections.
+
+## Fix Applied
+Changed the code to always update the config's host and port with the provided values:
+
+```cpp
+config_.host = std::move(host);
+config_.port = std::move(port);
+```
+
+## Changes Made
+**File**: `/testbed/include/ylt/coro_rpc/impl/coro_rpc_client.hpp`
+**Lines**: 330-331 (removed lines 330-335, replaced with 2 lines)
+
+## Testing Performed
+
+### 1. PR Scenario Test (`test_pr_scenario.cpp`)
+Replicates the exact scenario from the PR:
+- ✓ Connect to address A (127.0.0.1:19901)
+- ✓ Server A crashes
+- ✓ Connect to address B (127.0.0.1:19902)
+- ✓ Successfully communicate with server B
+
+**Result**: PASSED
+
+### 2. Comprehensive Test (`test_comprehensive.cpp`)
+Tests the main functionality:
+- ✓ Reconnect to different address after server crash
+- ✓ Reconnect to same address (regression test)
+
+**Result**: PASSED
+
+### 3. Edge Case Test (`test_edge_cases.cpp`)
+Tests various edge cases:
+- ✓ Connect with empty address (correctly fails)
+- ✓ Multiple sequential reconnections to different addresses
+- ✓ Reconnect back to a previously used address
+
+**Result**: PASSED
+
+## Impact Analysis
+
+### Fixed Behavior
+- Client can now connect to address A, close, then connect to address B (different address)
+- Config correctly updates to reflect the current connection target
+
+### Preserved Behavior
+- Reconnecting to the same address still works correctly
+- Empty address validation still works
+- Thread safety maintained via existing `connect_mutex_`
+
+### Breaking Changes
+None. The old behavior was a bug. Any code relying on it would be incorrect.
+
+## Use Cases Enabled
+1. **Failover**: Client can switch to backup server when primary crashes
+2. **Load Balancing**: Client can dynamically connect to different server instances
+3. **Service Discovery**: Client can follow address updates from service registry
+
+## Conclusion
+The fix is minimal, correct, and thoroughly tested. It resolves the issue described in the PR without introducing any breaking changes.

+# Fix for coro_rpc_client Reconnect to Different Address Issue
+
+## Problem
+The `coro_rpc_client` could not reconnect to a different address after the initial connection. 
+
+When calling `connect()` multiple times:
+1. First call to `connect("A")` - works correctly
+2. Close connection
+3. Second call to `connect("B")` - **BUG**: tries to connect to "A" instead of "B"
+
+This was because the config's host and port were only set if they were empty:
+
+```cpp
+if (config_.host.empty()) {
+    config_.host = std::move(host);
+}
+if (config_.port.empty()) {
+    config_.port = std::move(port);
+}
+```
+
+Once set during the first connection, they were never updated.
+
+## Solution
+Always update the config's host and port with the new values:
+
+```cpp
+config_.host = std::move(host);
+config_.port = std::move(port);
+```
+
+## Changes Made
+File: `/testbed/include/ylt/coro_rpc/impl/coro_rpc_client.hpp`
+
+Lines 330-335: Removed the empty check and always update host/port
+
+## Testing
+Created comprehensive tests that verify:
+
+1. **Main fix**: Client can connect to server A, close, then connect to server B (different address)
+2. **Regression test**: Client can still reconnect to the same address
+3. **Edge cases**: 
+   - Empty address correctly fails
+   - Multiple sequential reconnections to different addresses work
+   - Can reconnect back to a previous address
+
+All tests pass successfully.
+
+## Impact
+- **Fixes**: The bug described in the PR
+- **No breaking changes**: The old behavior was buggy; correct usage still works
+- **Thread safety**: Protected by existing `connect_mutex_`
+- **Backward compatible**: Reconnecting to the same address still works correctly
+
+## Use Case
+This fix enables important scenarios like:
+- Failover to backup servers when primary crashes
+- Load balancing across multiple server instances
+- Dynamic service discovery where the server address changes

+# Solution Summary: Fix for coro_rpc_client Reconnect Issue
+
+## Problem Description
+The `coro_rpc_client` could not reconnect to a different address after the initial connection. When attempting to connect to a new address B after being connected to address A, the client would try to reconnect to the old address A instead.
+
+## Root Cause
+In `/testbed/include/ylt/coro_rpc/impl/coro_rpc_client.hpp`, lines 330-335:
+```cpp
+if (config_.host.empty()) {
+    config_.host = std::move(host);
+}
+if (config_.port.empty()) {
+    config_.port = std::move(port);
+}
+```
+This code only updated the config's host and port if they were empty, preventing updates on subsequent connections.
+
+## Solution
+Removed the empty checks and always update the config:
+```cpp
+config_.host = std::move(host);
+config_.port = std::move(port);
+```
+
+## Code Changes
+**File**: `/testbed/include/ylt/coro_rpc/impl/coro_rpc_client.hpp`
+**Lines Modified**: 330-335 → 330-331
+**Lines Changed**: 6 lines removed, 2 lines added (net: -4 lines)
+
+## Testing
+Created three comprehensive test files:
+
+1. **test_pr_scenario.cpp** - Replicates exact PR scenario
+2. **test_comprehensive.cpp** - Tests main functionality and regressions
+3. **test_edge_cases.cpp** - Tests edge cases and multiple reconnections
+
+All tests pass successfully ✓
+
+## Verification
+```bash
+# Compile tests
+g++ -std=c++20 -I./include -I./include/ylt/thirdparty test_cmake/test_*.cpp -pthread
+
+# Run all tests
+./run_all_tests.sh
+```
+
+**Result**: All tests PASSED ✓
+
+## Impact
+- **Fixes**: The bug where client couldn't reconnect to different address
+- **Preserves**: Ability to reconnect to same address
+- **Enables**: Failover, load balancing, dynamic service discovery
+- **Breaking Changes**: None (old behavior was buggy)
+
+## Conclusion
+The fix is minimal (4 lines), correct, and thoroughly tested. It resolves the issue completely without introducing any breaking changes or regressions.

+/*
+ * Comprehensive test to verify that coro_rpc_client can reconnect to different addresses
+ * This test covers the scenarios described in the PR:
+ * 1. Connect to address A
+ * 2. Server A crashes (simulated)
+ * 3. Connect to address B (different from A)
+ * 4. Verify connection is to B, not A
+ */
+
+#include <ylt/coro_rpc/coro_rpc_client.hpp>
+#include <ylt/coro_rpc/coro_rpc_server.hpp>
+#include <async_simple/coro/SyncAwait.h>
+#include <iostream>
+#include <thread>
+#include <chrono>
+
+using namespace coro_rpc;
+using namespace async_simple::coro;
+using namespace std::chrono_literals;
+
+// Simple echo function for testing
+std::string echo(std::string msg) {
+    return msg;
+}
+
+bool test_reconnect_different_address() {
+    std::cout << "Test: Reconnect to different address" << std::endl;
+    
+    // Setup two servers on different ports
+    unsigned short port1 = 19801;
+    unsigned short port2 = 19802;
+    
+    coro_rpc_server server1(1, port1);
+    server1.register_handler<echo>();
+    auto res1 = server1.async_start();
+    if (res1.hasResult()) {
+        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Server1 couldn't start on port " << port1 << std::endl;
+        return false;
+    }
+    
+    coro_rpc_server server2(1, port2);
+    server2.register_handler<echo>();
+    auto res2 = server2.async_start();
+    if (res2.hasResult()) {
+        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Server2 couldn't start on port " << port2 << std::endl;
+        server1.stop();
+        return false;
+    }
+    
+    std::this_thread::sleep_for(100ms);  // Give servers time to start
+    
+    // Create client and connect to server1
+    coro_rpc_client client;
+    
+    std::cout << "  Step 1: Connect to server1 (127.0.0.1:" << port1 << ")" << std::endl;
+    auto ec1 = syncAwait(client.connect("127.0.0.1", std::to_string(port1)));
+    if (ec1) {
+        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Couldn't connect to server1: " << ec1.message() << std::endl;
+        server1.stop();
+        server2.stop();
+        return false;
+    }
+    
+    // Verify connected to the right server
+    std::string host1 = std::string(client.get_host());
+    std::string port1_str = std::string(client.get_port());
+    std::cout << "    Connected to: " << host1 << ":" << port1_str << std::endl;
+    if (port1_str != std::to_string(port1)) {
+        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Connected to wrong port!" << std::endl;
+        server1.stop();
+        server2.stop();
+        return false;
+    }
+    
+    // Test RPC call
+    auto result1 = syncAwait(client.call<echo>("test1"));
+    if (!result1) {
+        std::cerr << "  FAILED: RPC to server1 failed: " << result1.error().msg << std::endl;
+        server1.stop();
+        server2.stop();
+        return false;
+    }
+    std::cout << "    RPC result: " << result1.value() << std::endl;
+    
+    // Close connection and stop server1 (simulate crash)
+    std::cout << "  Step 2: Close connection and stop server1 (simulate crash)" << std::endl;
+    client.close();
+    server1.stop();
+    std::this_thread::sleep_for(100ms);
+    
+    // Try to reconnect to server2 (different address)
+    std::cout << "  Step 3: Connect to server2 (127.0.0.1:" << port2 << ")" << std::endl;
+    auto ec2 = syncAwait(client.connect("127.0.0.1", std::to_string(port2)));
+    if (ec2) {
+        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Couldn't connect to server2: " << ec2.message() << std::endl;
+        std::string current_host = std::string(client.get_host());
+        std::string current_port = std::string(client.get_port());
+        std::cerr << "    Client config shows: " << current_host << ":" << current_port << std::endl;
+        std::cerr << "    This indicates the bug: client tried to connect to old address!" << std::endl;
+        server2.stop();
+        return false;
+    }
+    
+    // Verify connected to the right server
+    std::string host2 = std::string(client.get_host());
+    std::string port2_str = std::string(client.get_port());
+    std::cout << "    Connected to: " << host2 << ":" << port2_str << std::endl;
+    if (port2_str != std::to_string(port2)) {
+        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Connected to wrong port! Expected " << port2 << " but got " << port2_str << std::endl;
+        server2.stop();
+        return false;
+    }
+    
+    // Test RPC call to verify we're actually connected to server2
+    auto result2 = syncAwait(client.call<echo>("test2"));
+    if (!result2) {
+        std::cerr << "  FAILED: RPC to server2 failed: " << result2.error().msg << std::endl;
+        server2.stop();
+        return false;
+    }
+    std::cout << "    RPC result: " << result2.value() << std::endl;
+    
+    client.close();
+    server2.stop();
+    
+    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
+    return true;
+}
+
+bool test_reconnect_same_address() {
+    std::cout << "Test: Reconnect to same address (regression test)" << std::endl;
+    
+    unsigned short port = 19803;
+    
+    coro_rpc_server server(1, port);
+    server.register_handler<echo>();
+    auto res = server.async_start();
+    if (res.hasResult()) {
+        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Server couldn't start on port " << port << std::endl;
+        return false;
+    }
+    
+    std::this_thread::sleep_for(100ms);
+    
+    coro_rpc_client client;
+    
+    // First connection
+    std::cout << "  Step 1: Initial connect" << std::endl;
+    auto ec1 = syncAwait(client.connect("127.0.0.1", std::to_string(port)));
+    if (ec1) {
+        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Initial connect failed: " << ec1.message() << std::endl;
+        server.stop();
+        return false;
+    }
+    
+    auto result1 = syncAwait(client.call<echo>("test1"));
+    if (!result1) {
+        std::cerr << "  FAILED: First RPC failed: " << result1.error().msg << std::endl;
+        server.stop();
+        return false;
+    }
+    std::cout << "    First RPC result: " << result1.value() << std::endl;
+    
+    // Close and reconnect to same address
+    std::cout << "  Step 2: Close and reconnect to same address" << std::endl;
+    client.close();
+    std::this_thread::sleep_for(50ms);
+    
+    auto ec2 = syncAwait(client.connect("127.0.0.1", std::to_string(port)));
+    if (ec2) {
+        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Reconnect failed: " << ec2.message() << std::endl;
+        server.stop();
+        return false;
+    }
+    
+    auto result2 = syncAwait(client.call<echo>("test2"));
+    if (!result2) {
+        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Second RPC failed: " << result2.error().msg << std::endl;
+        server.stop();
+        return false;
+    }
+    std::cout << "    Second RPC result: " << result2.value() << std::endl;
+    
+    client.close();
+    server.stop();
+    
+    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
+    return true;
+}
+
+int main() {
+    std::cout << "=== Testing coro_rpc_client reconnect to different address ===" << std::endl;
+    std::cout << std::endl;
+    
+    bool all_passed = true;
+    
+    all_passed &= test_reconnect_different_address();
+    std::cout << std::endl;
+    
+    all_passed &= test_reconnect_same_address();
+    std::cout << std::endl;
+    
+    if (all_passed) {
+        std::cout << "=== All tests PASSED ===" << std::endl;
+        return 0;
+    } else {
+        std::cout << "=== Some tests FAILED ===" << std::endl;
+        return 1;
+    }
+}

+/*
+ * Edge case test for the reconnect fix
+ */
+
+#include <ylt/coro_rpc/coro_rpc_client.hpp>
+#include <ylt/coro_rpc/coro_rpc_server.hpp>
+#include <async_simple/coro/SyncAwait.h>
+#include <iostream>
+#include <thread>
+#include <chrono>
+
+using namespace coro_rpc;
+using namespace async_simple::coro;
+using namespace std::chrono_literals;
+
+std::string echo(std::string msg) {
+    return msg;
+}
+
+bool test_connect_empty_address() {
+    std::cout << "Test: Connect with empty address (should fail)" << std::endl;
+    
+    coro_rpc_client client;
+    
+    // Try to connect with empty host/port
+    auto ec = syncAwait(client.connect("", ""));
+    if (ec == coro_rpc::errc::not_connected) {
+        std::cout << "  PASSED: Empty address correctly rejected" << std::endl;
+        return true;
+    } else {
+        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Empty address should have been rejected" << std::endl;
+        return false;
+    }
+}
+
+bool test_multiple_reconnects() {
+    std::cout << "Test: Multiple reconnects to different addresses" << std::endl;
+    
+    // Start three servers
+    unsigned short port1 = 19811;
+    unsigned short port2 = 19812;
+    unsigned short port3 = 19813;
+    
+    coro_rpc_server server1(1, port1);
+    server1.register_handler<echo>();
+    auto res1 = server1.async_start();
+    if (res1.hasResult()) {
+        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Server1 couldn't start" << std::endl;
+        return false;
+    }
+    
+    coro_rpc_server server2(1, port2);
+    server2.register_handler<echo>();
+    auto res2 = server2.async_start();
+    if (res2.hasResult()) {
+        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Server2 couldn't start" << std::endl;
+        server1.stop();
+        return false;
+    }
+    
+    coro_rpc_server server3(1, port3);
+    server3.register_handler<echo>();
+    auto res3 = server3.async_start();
+    if (res3.hasResult()) {
+        std::cerr << "  FAILED: Server3 couldn't start" << std::endl;
+        server1.stop();
+        server2.stop();
+        return false;
+    }
+    
+    std::this_thread::sleep_for(100ms);
+

+

+        server2.stop();
+        server3.stop();
